B000002H70|5.0|I feel inadequate that my most glowing review wouldn't do this album justice.  This is, quite simply and without exagerration, one of the greatest albums ever released.  It begins with the somber and moody opener Plainsong, and just continues to dazzle throughout the entire length of the album.  I particularly love its unhurried pace - more than a few songs begin with a lengthy and spectacular instrumental piece, as if Robert Smith is telling a beautiful story and is in no particular rush to get through it.  Instrumentally, Disintegration is sheer genius.  Electric guitar and synthesizer compliment each other perfectly throughout, with Simon Gallup's brilliant and underrated bass lines galvanizing the entire album, particularly in Fascination Street.  Pictures Of You is truly a classic, and instantly recognizable to anyone with even a passing interest in rock music coming out of the 80's.  Having said that, this album is not confined by the decade of its release.  It trancends any limitations that time and timely music would place upon it.  This album is truly enjoyable at any moment; past, present or future.  I usually list a handful of favorite songs from the album in my reviews, but I can't do that here - I love all of it.  Having come from The Cure, less enlightened listeners might dismiss it as a typical dreary and angst-driven album that their reputation would validate.  I, for one, have never dismissed The Cure is a 'doom and gloom' band, and I do not do so here.  In fact, I find this entire album laced with an undercurrent of hope - optimism that the clouds will part and the sun will soon shine through.  I will say with only the barest hint of facetiousness that if recorded music ceased to exist after the release of Disintegration, the art form would truly and greatly be fulfilled.  I hope you love this album as much as I have come to love it.  Thank you.

0525478817|5.0|***I WILL ATTEMPT TO KEEP THIS AS SPOILER FREE AS POSSIBLE***<br /><br />This is, without a doubt, one of the greatest novels I have ever read. That being for many reasons:<br /><br />1. The palpable emotions that this book conveys - I guarantee that you will laugh. I guarantee that you will cry. This incredible novel calls upon every human emotion and forces you to live the story. I will not hesitate to admit that I sobbed whilst reading this. I also laughed so hard that I had to take a moment to gather myself. If you don't like public displays of emotion, don't read this book outside the home.<br /><br />2. The characters are just so realistic - Enough said. There weren't many cliches (of course there were a few, cliches are EVERYWHERE and NO archetypes that I could see. No one was flawless, no one was so imperfect that no one could stand it. Everyone was the beautiful mixture of flaws and perfection. Not only this, their personalities were so realistic that they jumped off the page and sat right next to you as you read about their turmoils (for there are plenty of turmoils). You fall in love with characters, but there are also things about them that you can't stand. You come to despise characters, but their were things about them that you liked. Just like actual people, no?<br /><br />3. The story itself is VERY realistic - Again, self-explanatory. All these things could happen (in a way, they do happen). There aren't many corny coincidences (the ones that are there are beautifully explained), and everything is just so REAL. It has a realness to it that few other books capture. I can't find anything else to say about it other than, IT'S SO REAL.<br /><br />4. The narration - John Green does a beautiful job of putting us in Hazel's mind through her narrations. It's so perfect, I'm surprised it hasn't ascended to heaven. There were opinions (amazing), but not too many that we didn't get to form out own opinions (which sometimes happens with first person). Not onlywere scenes set beautifully and things explained fantastically, but you really got a teenagers voice. We didn't get an adult's pathetic attempt at trying to sound like an angsty teen. No, we got a teenager, a true teenager. It's incredible.<br /><br />5. Anything else that you could possibly fathom: IT HAS EVERYTHING: philosophy, romance, life, death, love, hate, excitement, disappointment, deepness, shallowness, and everything else. It is so incredible<br /><br />CITIQUES:<br />-At time it did get a tad bit philosophical (and by a tad bit, I mean a lot bit). If that's not your thing, push through it.<br />-References were made to \\"An Imperial Affliction\\" many times. I do not know if this book actually exists or not. It is explained well enough, but still. Too many referenced for my taste.<br />-I can't think of anything else, I just wanted more than two bullet points.<br /><br />All in all, this novel is incredible. It blows his previous work of Looking for Alaska out of the water (which is saying something because I consider Looking for Alaska one of the greatest novels of all time). I HIGHLY recommend it for ANYONE, for it is a must-read masterpiece made for anyone and everyone.
